The acceptance of repentance for the former group was revealed before that of the latter, and the latter were left in suspense regarding the acceptance of their repentance until the following verse was revealed, namely His saying: {Allah has certainly turned in forgiveness to the Prophet, and the Muhajirun and the Ansar} [al-Tawbah: 117] to the end of the verse, {and to the three who were left behind, until when the earth, with all its vastness, became too narrow for them, [and their own souls became too narrow for them]} [al-Tawbah: 118] to the end of the verse, as will come in the explanation in the hadith of Ka'b ibn Malik.

As for His saying, {Whether He punishes them or turns to them in mercy}, that is, they are under the pardon of Allah. If He wills, He does this with them, and if He wills, He does that with them, but His mercy prevails over His wrath. And He is {Knowing, Wise}, that is, Knowing of who deserves punishment among those who deserve pardon, Wise in His actions and His words. There is no god but He, and no lord besides Him.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ ومجاهدُ وعِكْرِمة، وَالضَّحَّاكُ وَغَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ: هُمُ الثَّلَاثَةُ الَّذِينَ خُلِّفُوا، أَيْ: عَنِ التَّوْبَةِ، وَهُمْ: مَرَارَةُ بْنُ الرَّبِيعِ، وَكَعْبُ بْنُ مَالِكٍ، وَهِلَالُ بْنُ أُمَيَّةَ، قَعَدُوا عَنْ غَزْوَةِ تَبُوكَ فِي جُمْلَةِ مَنْ قَعَدَ، كَسَلًا وَمَيْلًا إِلَى الدَّعَة وَالْحِفْظِ وَطَيِّبِ الثِّمَارِ وَالظِّلَالِ، لَا شَكًّا وَنِفَاقًا، فَكَانَتْ مِنْهُمْ طَائِفَةٌ رَبَطوا أَنْفُسَهُمْ بِالسَّوَارِي، كَمَا فَعَلَ أَبُو لُبابة وَأَصْحَابُهُ، وَطَائِفَةٌ لَمْ يَفْعَلُوا ذَلِكَ وَهُمْ هَؤُلَاءِ الثَّلَاثَةُ الْمَذْكُورُونَ، فَنَزَلَتْ تَوْبَةُ أُولَئِكَ قَبْلَ هَؤُلَاءِ، وَأَرْجَى هَؤُلَاءِ عَنِ التَّوْبَةِ حَتَّى نَزَلَتِ الْآيَةُ الْآتِيَةُ، وَهِيَ قَوْلُهُ: ﴿لَقَدْ تَابَ اللَّهُ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ وَالْمُهَاجِرِينَ وَالأنْصَارِ﴾ الْآيَةَ [التَّوْبَةِ: ١١٧] ، ﴿وَعَلَى الثَّلاثَةِ الَّذِينَ خُلِّفُوا حَتَّى إِذَا ضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الأرْضُ بِمَا رَحُبَتْ [وَضَاقَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ أَنْفُسُهُمْ] ﴾ الْآيَةَ [التَّوْبَةِ: ١١٨] ، كَمَا سَيَأْتِي بَيَانُهُ فِي حَدِيثِ كَعْبِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿إِمَّا يُعَذِّبُهُمْ وَإِمَّا يَتُوبُ عَلَيْهِمْ﴾ أَيْ: هُمْ تَحْتَ عَفْوِ اللَّهِ، إِنْ شَاءَ فَعَلَ بِهِمْ هَذَا، وَإِنْ شَاءَ فَعَلَ بِهِمْ ذَاكَ، وَلَكِنَّ رَحْمَتَهُ تَغْلِبُ غَضَبَهُ، وَهُوَ ﴿عَلِيمٌ حَكِيمٌ﴾ أَيْ: عَلِيمٌ بِمَنْ يَسْتَحِقُّ الْعُقُوبَةَ مِمَّنْ يَسْتَحِقُّ الْعَفْوَ، حَكِيمٌ فِي أَفْعَالِهِ وَأَقْوَالِهِ، لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ، وَلَا رَبَّ سِوَاهُ.

---

## 9:107-108 — verses 107-108 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The reason for the revelation of these noble verses is that there was in Medina, before the arrival of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, a man from Khazraj called "Abu Amir the Monk." He had become Christian during the Jahiliyyah (pre-Islamic period) and had studied the learning of the People of the Book. He had a reputation for worship in the Jahiliyyah, and he held great standing among Khazraj. When the Messenger of Allah ﷺ arrived as a migrant to Medina, and the Muslims gathered around him, and Islam attained a lofty position, and Allah made them victorious on the day of Badr, the accursed Abu Amir choked on his own spittle in resentment, openly declared enmity, and made it manifest. He fled out to the disbelievers of Mecca, among the polytheists of Quraysh, and incited them to war against the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. They gathered together with those Arab tribes who agreed with them and came in the year of Uhud. Then what happened to the Muslims happened, Allah tested them, and the final outcome belonged to the God-fearing.

This wicked man had dug pits between the two ranks, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ fell into one of them. He was struck that day: his face was wounded, his lower right canine tooth was broken, and his head was gashed ﷺ.

Abu Amir came forward at the start of the duel toward his people among the Ansar, addressed them, and tried to win them over to support and side with him. When they recognized his speech, they said, "May Allah not give your eye any comfort, O wicked one, O enemy of Allah," and they reviled and cursed him. He went back saying, "By Allah, evil has befallen my people after me." The Messenger of Allah ﷺ had called him to Allah before his flight and recited to him from the Qur'an, but he refused to accept Islam and remained defiant. So the Messenger of Allah ﷺ invoked against him that he should die far away, banished, and this supplication overtook him.

That was because when the people had finished with Uhud, and he saw the affair of the Messenger ﷺ, rising and prevailing, he went to Heraclius, the King of Rome, seeking his aid against the Prophet ﷺ. Heraclius made him promises and gave him false hopes, and he stayed with him. He wrote to a group of his people among the Ansar, among the people of hypocrisy and doubt, promising them and raising their hopes that he would soon come with an army to fight the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, defeat him, and turn him back from what he was engaged in. He ordered them to build for him a stronghold where whoever came from him to deliver his letters could arrive, and which would serve as a watch post for him when he himself came to them afterward. So they set about building a mosque adjacent to the mosque of Quba. They built it and made it solid, and finished it before the Prophet ﷺ set out for Tabuk. They came and asked the Messenger of Allah ﷺ to come to them and pray in their mosque, so that they could use his prayer there, peace be upon him, as evidence to establish and confirm it. They claimed that they had only built it for the weak among them and those with illness, for the cold, stormy night. But Allah protected him from praying in it, and he said, "We are on a journey, but when we return, if Allah wills."

When he, peace be upon him, was returning to Medina from Tabuk, with only a day or part of a day remaining before reaching it, revelation came down to him with news of the Mosque of Harm (masjid al-dirar) and what its builders had intended by way of disbelief and creating division among the community of believers regarding their mosque, the mosque of Quba, which had been founded from its first day upon piety. So the Messenger of Allah ﷺ sent someone to that mosque who demolished it before his own arrival in Medina, as Ali ibn Abi Talha reported from Ibn Abbas concerning His saying: {And those who took a mosque, causing harm and disbelief and division among the believers} They were people from the Ansar who built a mosque. Abu Amir had said to them, "Build a mosque and prepare as much strength and weapons as you can, for I am going to Caesar, the King of Rome, and I will bring troops from Rome and drive out Muhammad and his companions." When they finished building their mosque, they came to the Prophet ﷺ and said, "We have finished building our mosque, and we would like you to pray in it and invoke blessing for us." Then Allah, Mighty and Majestic, revealed: {Do not ever stand in it. A mosque founded upon piety from the first day} up to {And Allah does not guide the wrongdoing people}.

The same has been narrated from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, Mujahid, Urwah ibn al-Zubayr, Qatadah, and more than one of the scholars.

Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Yasar reported, from al-Zuhri, Yazid ibn Ruman, Abdullah ibn Abi Bakr, Asim ibn Umar ibn Qatadah, and others, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ, meaning on his way back from Tabuk, arrived and camped at Dhu Awan, a place an hour's journey by day from Medina. The people of the Mosque of Harm had come to him while he was preparing to set out for Tabuk and had said, "O Messenger of Allah, we have built a mosque for the sick, those in need, for the rainy night and the cold, stormy night, and we would like you to come to us and pray for us in it." He said, "I am in the midst of travel and preoccupied," or words to that effect as the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, "but when we return, if Allah, exalted is He, wills, we will come to you and pray for you in it." When he camped at Dhu Awan, news of the mosque reached him. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ then called Malik ibn al-Dukhshum, brother of Banu Salim ibn Awf, and Ma'n ibn Adi, or his brother Amir ibn Adi, brother of Bal'ijlan, and said, "Go to this mosque whose people are wrongdoers, and demolish it and burn it." They set out quickly until they reached Banu Salim ibn Awf, who were the clan of Malik ibn al-Dukhshum. Malik said to Ma'n, "Wait for me until I bring out fire from my household to you." He entered his household, took palm branches, and lit a fire in them. Then the two of them hurried on until they entered the mosque while its people were in it, and they burned it and demolished it, and its people scattered from it. Then there was revealed concerning them from the Qur'an what was revealed: {And those who took a mosque, causing harm and disbelief} to the end of the account. Those who had built it were twelve men: Khudham ibn Khalid, from Banu Ubayd ibn Zayd, one of Banu Amr ibn Awf, and it was from his house that the Mosque of Discord was carried out; Tha'labah ibn Hatib, from Banu Ubayd, affiliated to Banu Umayyah ibn Zayd; Mu'attib ibn Qushayr, from Banu Dubay'ah ibn Zayd; Abu Habibah ibn al-Adh'ar, from Banu Dubay'ah ibn Zayd; Abbad ibn Hunayf, brother of Sahl ibn Hunayf, from Banu Amr ibn Awf; Jariyah ibn Amir and his two sons Mujammi' ibn Jariyah and Zayd ibn Jariyah, and Nabtal ibn al-Harith, who were from Banu Dubay'ah; Bahzaj, who was from Banu Dubay'ah; Bijad ibn Uthman, who was from Banu Dubay'ah; and Wadi'ah ibn Thabit, affiliated to Banu Umayyah, of the clan of Abu Lubabah ibn Abd al-Mundhir.

Concerning His saying, {And they will surely swear}, meaning those who built it, {We intended nothing but good}, meaning, we did not intend by its construction anything but good and kindness toward the people. Allah, exalted is He, said: {And Allah bears witness that they are surely liars}, meaning, in what they aimed for and what they intended. They had built it only to cause harm to the mosque of Quba, and out of disbelief in Allah, and to create division among the believers, and as a watch post for one who had waged war against Allah and His Messenger, namely Abu Amir the wicked one, who was called "the Monk," may Allah curse him.

Concerning His saying, {Do not ever stand in it}, this is a prohibition from Allah to His Messenger ﷺ, with the community following him in this regard, against ever standing in it, meaning praying in it, ever.

Then He urged him to pray in the mosque of Quba, which had been founded from the first day of its construction upon piety, that is, obedience to Allah and obedience to His Messenger, and as a means of uniting the word of the believers and serving as a stronghold and refuge for Islam and its people. For this reason, He, exalted is He, said: {A mosque founded upon piety from the first day is more worthy that you should stand in it}. The context is specifically concerning the mosque of Quba. This is why it has come in an authentic hadith that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, "A prayer in the mosque of Quba is like an umrah." And in the Sahih, it is reported that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ used to visit the mosque of Quba both riding and walking. And in a hadith, it is mentioned that when the Messenger of Allah ﷺ built and established it upon his first arrival, while staying with Banu Amr ibn Awf, it was Gabriel who determined for him the direction of the qiblah. And Allah knows best.

Abu Dawud said: Muhammad ibn al-Ala narrated to us, Mu'awiyah ibn Hisham narrated to us, from Yunus ibn al-Harith, from Ibrahim ibn Abi Maymunah, from Abu Salih, from Abu Hurayrah, may Allah be pleased with him, from the Prophet ﷺ, who said: "This verse was revealed concerning the people of Quba: {In it are men who love to purify themselves}." He said: They used to cleanse themselves with water after relieving themselves, so the verse was revealed concerning them.

Al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah also narrated it, from the hadith of Yunus ibn al-Harith, who is weak, and al-Tirmidhi said: gharib (singular) from this route.

Al-Tabarani said: Al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Ma'mari related to us, Muhammad ibn Humayd al-Razi related to us, Salamah ibn al-Fadl related to us, from Muhammad ibn Ishaq, from al-A'mash, from Mujahid, from Ibn Abbas, who said: When this verse came down, {In it are men who love to purify themselves}, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ sent for Uwaym ibn Sa'idah and said: "What is this purification for which Allah has praised you?" He said: "O Messenger of Allah, no man or woman among us relieves himself without washing his private part," or he said, "his seat," and the Prophet ﷺ said: "This is it."

Imam Ahmad said: Husayn ibn Muhammad related to us, Abu Uways related to us, Shurahbil related to us, from Uwaym ibn Sa'idah al-Ansari, that he related to him that the Prophet ﷺ came to them in the mosque of Quba' and said: "Allah, Exalted is He, has praised you well concerning purification in the matter of your mosque. What is this purification you practice?" They said: "By Allah, O Messenger of Allah, we know of nothing except that we had neighbors among the Jews who used to wash their backsides after relieving themselves, so we washed as they washed."

Ibn Khuzaymah related it in his Sahih.

Hushaym said, from Abd al-Hamid al-Madani, from Ibrahim ibn Isma'il al-Ansari: that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to Uwaym ibn Sa'idah: "What is this for which Allah has praised you: {In it are men who love to purify themselves, and Allah loves those who purify themselves}?" They said: "O Messenger of Allah, we wash our backsides with water."

Ibn Jarir said: Muhammad ibn Umarah al-Asadi related to me, Muhammad ibn Sa'd related to us, Ibrahim ibn Muhammad related to us, from Shurahbil ibn Sa'd, who said: I heard Khuzaymah ibn Thabit say: This verse came down, {In it are men who love to purify themselves, and Allah loves those who purify themselves}. He said: They used to wash their backsides after relieving themselves.

Another hadith: Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal said: Yahya ibn Adam related to us, Malik, that is, ibn Mighwal, related to us, I heard Sayyar Abu al-Hakam, from Shahr ibn Hawshab, from Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Salam, who said: When the Messenger of Allah ﷺ arrived, meaning at Quba', he said: "Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has praised you well concerning purification. Will you not tell me?" meaning His saying, Exalted is He: {In it are men who love to purify themselves, and Allah loves those who purify themselves}. They said: "O Messenger of Allah, we find it written upon us in the Torah: cleansing oneself after relieving oneself with water."

A group of the early generations have stated explicitly that it was the mosque of Quba'. This was related by Ali ibn Abi Talhah, from Ibn Abbas. It was also related by Abd al-Razzaq, from Ma'mar, from al-Zuhri, from Urwah ibn al-Zubayr. Atiyyah al-Awfi, Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam, al-Sha'bi, and al-Hasan al-Basri said the same, and al-Baghawi transmitted it from Sa'id ibn Jubayr and Qatadah.

It has come in the authentic hadith that the mosque of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, which is within the city of Medina itself, is the mosque that was founded upon piety. This is authentic, and there is no contradiction between the verse and this, because if the mosque of Quba' was founded upon piety from its very first day, then the mosque of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ is even more deserving and more fitting of that description. This is why Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal said in his Musnad:

Abu Nu'aym related to us, Abd Allah ibn Amir al-Aslami related to us, from Imran ibn Abi Anas, from Sahl ibn Sa'd, from Ubayy ibn Ka'b: that the Prophet ﷺ said: "The mosque that was founded upon piety is this mosque of mine." Ahmad alone related this.

Another hadith: Imam Ahmad said: Waki' related to us, Rabi'ah ibn Uthman al-Taymi related to us, from Imran ibn Abi Anas, from Sahl ibn Sa'd al-Sa'idi, who said: Two men disputed in the time of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ about the mosque that was founded upon piety. One of them said it was the mosque of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and the other said it was the mosque of Quba'.

They came to the Prophet ﷺ and asked him, and he said: "It is this mosque of mine." Ahmad alone related this as well.

Another hadith: Ahmad said: Musa ibn Dawud related to us, Layth related to us, from Imran ibn Abi Anas, from Sa'id ibn Abi Sa'id al-Khudri, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: Two men disputed about the mosque that was founded upon piety. One of them said it was the mosque of Quba', and the other said it was the mosque of the Prophet ﷺ. The Prophet ﷺ said: "It is this mosque of mine." Ahmad alone related this.

Another route: Imam Ahmad said: Ishaq ibn Isa related to us, Layth related to us, Imran ibn Abi Anas related to me, from Ibn Abi Sa'id, from his father, that he said: Two men disputed about the mosque that was founded upon piety from its first day. One man said it was the mosque of Quba', and the other said it was the mosque of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "It is my mosque."

Al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i related it likewise from Qutaybah, from Layth, and al-Tirmidhi judged it authentic. Muslim also related it, as will be seen.

Another route: Ahmad said: Yahya related to us, from Unays ibn Abi Yahya, my father related to me, who said: I heard Abu Sa'id al-Khudri say: Two men disputed, a man from Banu Khadrah and a man from Banu Amr ibn Awf, about the mosque that was founded upon piety. Al-Khudri said it was the mosque of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and the man from Amr said it was the mosque of Quba'. They came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and asked him about that, and he said: "It is this mosque," meaning the mosque of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and he said: "In that one," meaning the mosque of Quba', "there is much good."

Another route: Abu Ja'far ibn Jarir said: Ibn Bashshar related to us, Yahya ibn Sa'id related to us, Humayd al-Khurrat al-Madani related to us: I asked Abu Salamah ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Sa'id, saying: How did you hear your father speak about the mosque that was founded upon piety? He said, my father said: I came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and entered upon him in the house of one of his wives, and I said: "O Messenger of Allah, where is the mosque that was founded upon piety?" He said: he took a handful of pebbles and struck the ground with it, then said: "It is this mosque of yours." Then he said: [I said to him: Is this] how you heard your father mention it?

Muslim related this alone, from Muhammad ibn Hatim, from Yahya ibn Sa'id, with this chain, and he also related it from Abu Bakr ibn Abi Shaybah and others, from Hatim ibn Isma'il, from Humayd al-Khurrat, with this chain.

A group of the earlier and later scholars held that it was the mosque of the Prophet ﷺ, and this is related from Umar ibn al-Khattab, his son Abd Allah, Zayd ibn Thabit, and Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib. Ibn Jarir preferred this view.

His saying, Exalted is He: {A mosque founded upon piety from the first day is more worthy that you should stand in it. In it are men who love to purify themselves, and Allah loves those who purify themselves} is evidence for the desirability of praying in old mosques that were founded from the very first of their construction upon the worship of Allah alone, without partner, and for the desirability of praying together with the congregation of the righteous and the worshippers who act rightly, who maintain the thoroughness of ablution and who keep themselves clear of contact with filth.

Imam Ahmad said: Muhammad ibn Ja'far related to us, from Shu'bah, from Abd al-Malik ibn Umayr, I heard Shabib Abu Rawh relate from a man among the companions of the Prophet ﷺ, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ led them in the dawn prayer and recited to them Surah al-Rum, and he became confused. When he finished, he said: "The Qur'an becomes confused for us. Indeed some of you who pray with us do not perform ablution well. Whoever attends the prayer with us should perform the ablution well."

Then he related it through two other routes, from Abd al-Malik ibn Umayr, from Shabib Abu Rawh of Dhu al-Kala', that he prayed with the Prophet ﷺ, and he mentioned it. This indicates that completing one's purification makes it easier to stand in worship, and helps one to complete it fully and to fulfill what is prescribed in it.

Abu al-Aliyah said concerning His saying, Exalted is He: {And Allah loves those who purify themselves}: Purification with water is indeed good, but they are those who purify themselves from sins.

Al-A'mash said: Repentance is from sin, and purification is from associating partners with Allah (shirk).

It has come in the hadith related through several routes, in the Sunan and other collections, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to the people of Quba': "Allah has praised you concerning purification. What do you do?" They said: "We cleanse ourselves after relieving ourselves with water."

The Hafiz Abu Bakr al-Bazzar said: [chain] Abdullah ibn Shabib told us, Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Abd al-Aziz told us, saying: I found it in my father's book, from al-Zuhri, from Ubaydullah ibn Abdullah, from Ibn Abbas, who said: this verse was revealed concerning the people of Quba. {In it are men who love to purify themselves, and Allah loves those who purify themselves.} The Messenger of Allah ﷺ asked them about this, and they said: we follow up the use of stones with water.

Then he said: Muhammad ibn Abd al-Aziz alone transmitted this from al-Zuhri, and no one narrated from him except his son. I say: I have mentioned it in this wording because it is well known among the jurists, though many of the later hadith scholars, or perhaps all of them, are not familiar with it. And Allah knows best.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

سَبَبُ نُزُولِ هَذِهِ الْآيَاتِ الْكَرِيمَاتِ: أَنَّهُ كَانَ بِالْمَدِينَةِ قَبْلَ مَقدَم رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ إِلَيْهَا رَجُلٌ مِنَ الْخَزْرَجِ يُقَالُ لَهُ: "أَبُو عَامِرٍ الراهبُ"، وَكَانَ قَدْ تَنَصَّر فِي الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ وَقَرَأَ علْم أَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ، وَكَانَ فِيهِ عِبَادَةٌ فِي الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ، وَلَهُ شَرَفٌ فِي الْخَزْرَجِ كَبِيرٌ. فَلَمَّا قَدم رسولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ مُهَاجِرًا إِلَى الْمَدِينَةِ، وَاجْتَمَعَ الْمُسْلِمُونَ عَلَيْهِ، وَصَارَتْ لِلْإِسْلَامِ كَلِمَةٌ عَالِيَةٌ، وَأَظْهَرَهُمُ اللَّهُ يَوْمَ بَدْرٍ، شَرِق اللَّعِينُ أَبُو عَامِرٍ بِرِيقِهِ، وَبَارَزَ بِالْعَدَاوَةِ، وَظَاهَرَ بِهَا، وَخَرَجَ فَارًّا إِلَى كُفَّارِ مَكَّةَ مِنْ مُشْرِكِي قُرَيْشٍ فألَّبهم عَلَى حَرْبِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ، فَاجْتَمَعُوا بِمَنْ وَافَقَهُمْ مِنْ أَحْيَاءِ الْعَرَبِ، وَقَدِمُوا عَامَ أُحُدٍ، فَكَانَ مِنْ أَمْرِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ مَا كَانَ، وَامْتَحَنَهُمُ اللَّهُ، وَكَانَتِ الْعَاقِبَةُ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ. 

وَكَانَ هَذَا الْفَاسِقُ قَدْ حَفَرَ حَفَائِرَ فِيمَا بَيْنَ الصَّفَّيْنِ، فَوَقَعَ فِي إِحْدَاهُنَّ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ، وَأُصِيبَ ذَلِكَ الْيَوْمَ، فَجُرِحَ فِي وَجْهِهِ وكُسِرت ربَاعِيتُه الْيُمْنَى السُّفْلَى، وشُجَّ رَأْسُهُ، صَلَوَاتُ اللَّهِ وَسَلَامُهُ عَلَيْهِ.

وَتَقَدَّمَ أَبُو عَامِرٍ فِي أَوَّلِ الْمُبَارَزَةِ إِلَى قَوْمِهِ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ، فَخَاطَبَهُمْ وَاسْتَمَالَهُمْ إِلَى نَصْرِهِ وَمُوَافَقَتِهِ، فَلَمَّا عَرَفُوا كَلَامَهُ قَالُوا: لَا أَنْعَمَ اللَّهُ بِكَ عَيْنًا يَا فَاسِقُ يَا عَدُوَّ اللَّهِ، وَنَالُوا مِنْهُ وسبُّوه. فَرَجَعَ وَهُوَ يَقُولُ: وَاللَّهِ لَقَدْ أَصَابَ قَوْمِي بَعْدِي شَر. وَكَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَدْ دَعَاهُ إِلَى اللَّهِ قَبْلَ فِرَارِهِ، وَقَرَأَ عَلَيْهِ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ، فَأَبَى أَنْ يُسْلِمَ وتمرَّد، فَدَعَا عَلَيْهِ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَنْ يَمُوتَ بَعِيدًا طَرِيدًا، فَنَالَتْهُ هَذِهِ الدَّعْوَةُ.

وَذَلِكَ أَنَّهُ لَمَّا فَرَغَ النَّاسُ مِنْ أُحُدٍ، وَرَأَى أَمْرَ الرَّسُولِ، صَلَوَاتُ اللَّهِ وَسَلَامُهُ عَلَيْهِ فِي ارْتِفَاعٍ وَظُهُورٍ، ذَهَبَ إِلَى هِرَقْلَ، مَلِكِ الرُّومِ، يَسْتَنْصِرُهُ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ ﷺ، فَوَعَدَهُ ومَنَّاه، وَأَقَامَ عِنْدَهُ، وَكَتَبَ إِلَى جَمَاعَةٍ مِنْ قَوْمِهِ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ مِنْ أَهْلِ النِّفَاقِ وَالرَّيْبِ يَعِدُهُمْ ويُمنَّيهم أَنَّهُ سيقدمُ بِجَيْشٍ يُقَاتِلُ بِهِ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ وَيَغْلِبُهُ وَيَرُدُّهُ عَمَّا هُوَ فِيهِ، وَأَمَرَهُمْ أَنْ يَتَّخِذُوا لَهُ مَعقلا يَقْدَمُ عَلَيْهِمْ فِيهِ مَنْ يَقْدَمُ مِنْ عِنْدِهِ لِأَدَاءِ كُتُبه ويكونَ مَرْصَدًا لَهُ إِذَا قَدِمَ عَلَيْهِمْ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ، فَشَرَعُوا فِي بِنَاءِ مَسْجِدٍ مُجَاوِرٍ لِمَسْجِدِ قُبَاءٍ، فَبَنَوْهُ وَأَحْكَمُوهُ، وَفَرَغُوا مِنْهُ قَبْلَ خُرُوجِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ إِلَى تَبُوكَ، وَجَاءُوا فَسَأَلُوا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ أَنْ يَأْتِيَ إِلَيْهِمْ فَيُصَلِّيَ فِي مَسْجِدِهِمْ، لِيَحْتَجُّوا بِصَلَاتِهِ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، فِيهِ عَلَى تَقْرِيرِهِ وَإِثْبَاتِهِ، وَذَكَرُوا أَنَّهُمْ إِنَّمَا بَنَوْهُ لِلضُّعَفَاءِ مِنْهُمْ وَأَهْلِ الْعِلَّةِ فِي اللَّيْلَةِ الشَّاتِيَةِ، فَعَصَمَهُ اللَّهُ مِنَ الصَّلَاةِ فِيهِ فَقَالَ: "إِنَّا عَلَى سَفَرٍ، وَلَكِنْ إِذَا رَجَعْنَا إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ".

فَلَمَّا قَفَلَ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ رَاجِعًا إِلَى الْمَدِينَةِ مِنْ تَبُوكَ، وَلَمْ يَبْقَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَهَا إِلَّا يَوْمٌ أَوْ بَعْضُ يَوْمٍ، نَزَلَ عَلَيْهِ الْوَحْيُ بِخَبَرِ مَسْجِدِ الضِّرار، وَمَا اعْتَمَدَهُ بَانُوهُ مِنَ الْكُفْرِ وَالتَّفْرِيقِ بَيْنَ جَمَاعَةِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فِي مَسْجِدِهِمْ مَسْجِدِ قُبَاءَ، الَّذِي أُسِّسَ مِنْ أَوَّلِ يَوْمٍ عَلَى التَّقْوَى. فَبَعَثَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ إِلَى ذَلِكَ الْمَسْجِدِ مَنْ هَدَمه قَبْلَ مَقْدَمِهِ الْمَدِينَةَ، كَمَا قَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابن عباس فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ اتَّخَذُوا مَسْجِدًا ضِرَارًا [وَكُفْرًا وَتَفْرِيقًا بَيْنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ] ﴾ وَهُمْ أُنَاسٌ مِنَ الْأَنْصَارِ، ابْتَنَوْا مَسْجِدًا، فَقَالَ لَهُمْ أَبُو عَامِرٍ، ابْنُوا مَسْجِدًا وَاسْتَعِدُّوا بِمَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ مِنْ قُوَّةٍ وَمِنْ سِلَاحٍ، فَإِنِّي ذَاهِبٌ إِلَى قَيْصَرَ مَلِكِ الرُّومِ، فَآتِي بِجُنْدٍ مِنَ الرُّومِ وَأُخْرِجُ مُحَمَّدًا وَأَصْحَابَهُ. فَلَمَّا فَرَغُوا مِنْ مَسْجِدِهِمْ أَتَوُا النَّبِيَّ ﷺ فَقَالُوا: قَدْ فَرَغْنَا مِنْ بِنَاءِ مَسْجِدِنَا، فَنُحِبُّ أَنْ تُصَلِيَ فِيهِ وَتَدْعُوَ لَنَا بِالْبَرَكَةِ. فَأَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: ﴿لَا تَقُمْ فِيهِ أَبَدًا لَمَسْجِدٌ أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى مِنْ أَوَّلِ يَوْمٍ﴾ إِلَى ﴿وَاللَّهُ لَا يَهْدِي الْقَوْمَ الظَّالِمِينَ﴾ .

وَكَذَا رُوي عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبير، وَمُجَاهِدٍ، وَعُرْوَةَ بْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ، وَقَتَادَةَ وَغَيْرِ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْعُلَمَاءِ.

وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ بْنِ يَسَار، عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، وَيَزِيدَ بْنِ رُومَانَ، وعبد الله بن أبي بكر، وعاصم بن عُمَر بن قتادة وغيرهم، قالوا: أَقْبَلَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ -يَعْنِي: مِنْ تَبُوكَ -حَتَّى نَزَلَ بِذِي أَوَانٍ -بَلَدٌ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْمَدِينَةِ سَاعَةٌ مِنْ نَهَارٍ -وَكَانَ أَصْحَابُ مَسْجِدِ الضِّرَارِ قَدْ كَانُوا أَتَوْهُ وَهُوَ يَتَجَهَّزُ إِلَى تَبُوكَ، فَقَالُوا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّا قَدْ بَنَيْنَا مَسْجِدًا لِذِي الْعِلَّةِ وَالْحَاجَةِ، وَاللَّيْلَةِ الْمَطِيرَةِ، وَاللَّيْلَةِ الشَّاتِيَةِ، وَإِنَّا نُحِبُّ أَنْ تَأْتِيَنَا فَتُصِلِّيَ لَنَا فِيهِ. فَقَالَ: "إِنِّي عَلَى جَنَاحِ سَفر وَحَالِ شُغل -أَوْ كَمَا قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ -وَلَوْ قَدْ قَدِمْنَا إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى أَتَيْنَاكُمْ فَصَلَّيْنَا لَكُمْ فِيهِ". فَلَمَّا نَزَلَ بِذِي أَوَانٍ أَتَاهُ خبرُ الْمَسْجِدِ، فَدَعَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ مَالِكَ بْنَ الدُّخْشُم أَخَا بَنِي سَالِمِ بْنِ عَوْفٍ، وَمَعْنَ بْنَ عَدِيٍّ -أَوْ: أَخَاهُ عَامِرِ بْنِ عَدِيٍّ -أَخَا بَلْعِجْلَانَ فَقَالَ: "انْطَلِقَا إِلَى هَذَا الْمَسْجِدِ الظَّالِمِ أَهْلُهُ، فَاهْدِمَاهُ وَحَرِّقَاهُ". فَخَرَجَا سَرِيعَيْنِ حَتَّى أَتَيَا بَنِي سَالِمِ بْنِ عَوْفٍ، وَهُمْ رَهْطُ مَالِكِ بْنِ الدُّخْشُمَ، فَقَالَ مَالِكٌ لِمَعْنٍ: أَنْظِرْنِي حَتَّى أَخْرُجَ إِلَيْكَ بِنَارٍ مِنْ أَهْلِي. فَدَخَلَ أَهْلَهُ فَأَخَذَ سَعَفا مِنَ النَّخْلِ، فَأَشْعَلَ فِيهِ نَارًا، ثُمَّ خَرَجَا يَشتدَّان حَتَّى دَخَلَا الْمَسْجِدَ وَفِيهِ أَهْلُهُ، فَحَرَقَاهُ وَهَدَمَاهُ وَتَفَرَّقُوا عَنْهُ. وَنَزَلَ فِيهِمْ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ مَا نَزَلَ: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ اتَّخَذُوا مَسْجِدًا ضِرَارًا وَكُفْرًا﴾ إِلَى آخِرِ الْقِصَّةِ. وَكَانَ الَّذِينَ بَنَوْهُ اثْنَيْ عَشَرَ رَجُلًا خُذَامُ بْنُ خَالِدٍ، مِنْ بَنِي عُبَيد بْنِ زَيْدٍ، أَحَدُ بَنِي عَمْرِو بْنِ عَوْفٍ، وَمِنْ دَارِهِ أُخْرِجَ مَسْجِدُ الشِّقَاقِ، وَثَعْلَبَةُ بْنُ حَاطِبٍ مِنْ بَنِي عُبَيْدٍ وَهُوَ إِلَى بَنِي أُمَيَّةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ، ومعتِّب بْنُ قُشير، مِنْ [بَنِي] ضُبَيعة بْنِ زَيْدٍ، وَأَبُو حَبِيبَةَ بْنُ الْأَذْعَرِ، مِنْ بَنِي ضُبَيعة بْنِ زَيْدٍ، وعَبَّاد بْنُ حُنَيف، أَخُو سَهْلِ بْنِ حُنَيْفٍ، مِنْ بَنِي عَمْرِو بْنِ عَوْفٍ، وَجَارِيَةُ بْنُ عَامِرٍ، وَابْنَاهُ: مُجَمِّع بْنُ جَارِيَةَ، وَزَيْدُ بْنُ جَارِيَةَ ونَبْتَل [بْنُ] الْحَارِثِ، وَهُمْ مِنْ بَنِي ضُبَيْعَةَ، وَبَحْزَجٌ وَهُوَ مِنْ بَنِي ضُبَيْعَةَ، وَبِجَادُ بْنُ عُثمان وَهُوَ مِنْ بَنِي ضُبَيعة، [وَوَدِيعَةُ بْنُ ثَابِتٍ، وَهُوَ إِلَى بَنِي أُمَيَّةَ] رَهْطُ أَبِي لَبَابَةَ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْمُنْذِرِ. 

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَلَيَحْلِفُنَّ﴾ أَيْ: الَّذِينَ بَنَوْهُ ﴿إِنْ أَرَدْنَا إِلا الْحُسْنَى﴾ أَيْ: مَا أَرَدْنَاهُ بِبُنْيَانِهِ إِلَّا خَيْرًا وَرِفْقًا بِالنَّاسِ، قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَاللَّهُ يَشْهَدُ إِنَّهُمْ لَكَاذِبُونَ﴾ أَيْ: فِيمَا قَصَدُوا وَفِيمَا نوَوا، وَإِنَّمَا بَنُوهُ ضِرارا لِمَسْجِدِ قُباء، وَكَفْرًا بِاللَّهِ، وَتَفْرِيقًا بَيْنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، وَإِرْصَادًا لِمَنْ حَارَبَ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ، وَهُوَ أَبُو عَامِرٍ الْفَاسِقُ، الَّذِي يُقَالُ لَهُ: "الرَّاهِبُ" لَعَنَهُ اللَّهُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿لَا تَقُمْ فِيهِ أَبَدًا﴾ نَهْيٌ مِنَ اللَّهِ لِرَسُولِهِ، صَلَوَاتُ اللَّهِ وَسَلَامُهُ عَلَيْهِ، وَالْأُمَّةُ تَبَع لَهُ فِي ذَلِكَ، عَنْ أَنْ يَقُومَ فِيهِ، أَيْ: يُصَلِّي فِيهِ أَبَدًا.

ثُمَّ حَثَّهُ عَلَى الصَّلَاةِ فِي مَسْجِدِ قُباء الَّذِي أُسِّسَ مِنْ أَوَّلِ يَوْمِ بِنَائِهِ عَلَى التَّقْوَى، وَهِيَ طَاعَةُ اللَّهِ، وَطَاعَةُ رَسُولِهِ، وَجَمْعًا لِكَلِمَةِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ ومَعقلا وَمَوْئِلًا لِلْإِسْلَامِ وَأَهْلِهِ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿لَمَسْجِدٌ أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى مِنْ أَوَّلِ يَوْمٍ أَحَقُّ أَنْ تَقُومَ فِيهِ﴾ وَالسِّيَاقُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ فِي مَعْرِضِ مسجد قباء؛ ولهذا جاء فِي الْحَدِيثِ الصَّحِيحِ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: "صَلَاةٌ فِي مَسْجِدِ قُباء كعُمرة". وَفِي الصَّحِيحِ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ كَانَ يزورُ مَسْجِدَ قُباء رَاكِبًا وَمَاشِيًا وَفِي الْحَدِيثِ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ لَمَّا بَنَاهُ وَأَسَّسَهُ أَوَّلَ قُدُومِهِ وَنُزُولِهِ عَلَى بَنِي عَمْرِو بْنِ عَوْفٍ، كَانَ جِبْرِيلُ هُوَ الَّذِي عَيَّن لَهُ جِهَة الْقِبْلَةِ فَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

وَقَالَ أَبُو دَاوُدَ: حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ الْعَلَاءِ، حَدَّثَنَا مُعَاوِيَةُ بْنُ هِشَامٍ، عَنْ يُونُسَ بْنِ الْحَارِثِ، عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ بْنِ أَبِيَ مَيْمُونَةَ، عَنْ أَبِي صَالِحٍ، عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وسلم قال: "نزلت هَذِهِ الْآيَةُ فِي أَهْلِ قُبَاءٍ: ﴿فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا﴾ قَالَ: كَانُوا يَسْتَنْجُونَ بِالْمَاءِ، فَنَزَلَتْ فِيهِمُ الْآيَةُ.

وَرَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ يُونُسَ بْنِ الْحَارِثِ، وَهُوَ ضَعِيفٌ، وَقَالَ التِّرْمِذِيُّ: غَرِيبٌ مِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ.

وَقَالَ الطَّبَرَانِيُّ: حَدَّثَنَا الْحَسَنُ بْنُ عَلِيٍّ الْمَعْمَرِيُّ، حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ حُمَيْدٍ الرَّازِيُّ، حَدَّثَنَا سَلَمَةُ بْنُ الْفَضْلِ، عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ إِسْحَاقَ، عَنِ الْأَعْمَشِ، عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: لَمَّا نَزَلَتْ هَذِهِ الْآيَةُ: ﴿فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا﴾ بَعَثَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ إِلَى عُوَيم بْنِ سَاعِدَةَ فَقَالَ: "مَا هَذَا الطَّهُورُ الَّذِي أَثْنَى اللَّهُ عَلَيْكُمْ؟ ". فَقَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، مَا خَرَجَ مِنَّا رَجُلٌ وَلَا امْرَأَةٌ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ إِلَّا غَسَلَ فَرْجَهُ -أَوْ قَالَ: مَقْعَدَتَهُ -فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ. "هُوَ هَذَا". 

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا حُسَين بْنُ مُحَمَّدٍ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو أُوَيْسٍ، حَدَّثَنَا شُرَحْبِيلُ، عَنْ عُوَيم بْنِ سَاعِدَةَ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ: أَنَّهُ حَدّثه أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ أَتَاهُمْ فِي مَسْجِدِ قُباء، فَقَالَ: "إِنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى قَدْ أَحْسَنَ [عَلَيْكُمُ الثَّنَاءَ] فِي الطَّهور فِي قِصَّةِ مَسْجِدِكُمْ، فَمَا هَذَا الطَّهُورُ الَّذِي تَطَهَّرُونَ بِهِ؟ " فَقَالُوا: وَاللَّهِ -يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ -مَا نَعْلَمُ شَيْئًا إِلَّا أَنَّهُ كَانَ لَنَا جِيرَانٌ مِنَ الْيَهُودِ، فَكَانُوا يَغْسِلُونَ أَدْبَارَهُمْ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ، فَغَسَلْنَا كَمَا غَسَلُوا.

وَرَوَاهُ ابْنُ خُزيمة فِي صَحِيحِهِ. 

وَقَالَ هُشَيْم، عَنْ عَبْدِ الْحَمِيدِ الْمَدَنِيِّ، عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ بْنِ إِسْمَاعِيلَ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وسلم قال لعُوَيم بْنِ سَاعِدَةَ. "مَا هَذَا الَّذِي أَثْنَى اللَّهُ عَلَيْكُمْ: ﴿فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُطَّهِّرِينَ﴾ قَالُوا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّا نَغْسِلُ الْأَدْبَارَ بِالْمَاءِ. 

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنِي مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ عُمارة الْأَسَدِيُّ، حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ سَعْدٍ، حَدَّثَنَا إِبْرَاهِيمُ بْنُ مُحَمَّدٍ، عَنْ شُرَحْبِيلَ بْنِ سَعْدٍ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ خُزَيمة بْنِ ثَابِتٍ يَقُولُ: نَزَلَتْ هَذِهِ الْآيَةُ: ﴿فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُطَّهِّرِينَ﴾ قَالَ: كَانُوا يَغْسِلُونَ أَدْبَارَهُمْ مِنَ الْغَائِطِ. 

حَدِيثٌ آخَرُ: قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ بْنُ حَنْبَلٍ: حَدَّثَنَا يَحْيَى بْنُ آدَمَ، حَدَّثَنَا مَالِكٌ -يَعْنِي: ابْنَ مغْوَل -سَمِعْتُ سَيَّارًا أَبَا الْحَكَمِ، عَنْ شَهْرِ بْنِ حَوْشَبٍ، عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ سَلَامٍ قَالَ: لَمَّا قَدِمَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ، يَعْنِي: قُبَاءَ، فَقَالَ: "إِنَّ اللَّهَ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، قَدْ أَثْنَى عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الطَّهُورِ خَيْرًا، أَفَلَا تُخْبِرُونِي؟ ". يَعْنِي: قَوْلَهُ تَعَالَى: ﴿فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُطَّهِّرِينَ﴾ فَقَالُوا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِنَّا نَجِدُهُ مَكْتُوبًا عَلَيْنَا فِي التَّوْرَاةِ: الاستنجاءُ بِالْمَاءِ. 

وَقَدْ صَرَّحَ بِأَنَّهُ مَسْجِدُ قُبَاءٍ جَمَاعَةٌ مِنَ السَّلَفِ، رَوَاهُ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ. وَرَوَاهُ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، عَنْ مَعْمَر، عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، عَنْ عُرْوَة بْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ. وَقَالَهُ عَطِيَّةُ الْعَوْفِيُّ، وَعَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ، وَالشَّعْبِيُّ، وَالْحَسَنُ الْبَصْرِيُّ، وَنَقَلَهُ الْبَغَوِيُّ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَير، وَقَتَادَةَ.

وَقَدْ وَرَدَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ الصَّحِيحِ: أَنَّ مَسْجِدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ الَّذِي هُوَ فِي جَوْفِ الْمَدِينَةِ، هُوَ الْمَسْجِدُ الَّذِي أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى. وَهَذَا صَحِيحٌ. وَلَا مُنَافَاةَ بَيْنَ الْآيَةِ وَبَيْنَ هَذَا؛ لِأَنَّهُ إِذَا كَانَ مَسْجِدُ قُبَاءٍ قَدْ أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى مِنْ أَوَّلِ يَوْمٍ، فَمَسْجِدُ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ بِطَرِيقِ الْأَوْلَى وَالْأَحْرَى؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ بْنُ حَنْبَلٍ فِي مُسْنَدِهِ:

حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو نُعيم، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ عَامِرٍ الْأَسْلَمِيُّ، عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ أَبِي أَنَسٍ، عَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ، عَنْ أُبَيِّ بْنِ كَعْبٍ: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ: "الْمَسْجِدُ الَّذِي أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى مَسْجِدِي هَذَا". تَفَرَّدَ بِهِ أَحْمَدُ. 

حَدِيثٌ آخَرُ: قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا وَكِيع، حَدَّثَنَا رَبِيعَةُ بْنُ عُثْمَانَ التَّيْمِيُّ، عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ أَبِي أَنَسٍ، عَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ السَّاعِدِيِّ قَالَ: اخْتَلَفَ رَجُلَانِ عَلَى عَهْدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الَّذِي أسِّسَ على التقوى، فقال أحدهما: هو مَسْجِدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ. وقال الآخر: هو مسجد قباء.

فَأَتَيَا النَّبِيَّ ﷺ فَسَأَلَاهُ، فَقَالَ: "هُوَ مَسْجِدِي هَذَا" تَفَرَّدَ بِهِ أَحْمَدُ أَيْضًا.

حَدِيثٌ آخَرُ: قَالَ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا مُوسَى بْنُ دَاوُدَ، حَدَّثَنَا لَيْثٌ، عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ أَبِي أَنَسٍ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: تَمَارَى رَجُلَانِ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الَّذِي أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى، فَقَالَ أَحَدُهُمَا: هُوَ مَسْجِدُ قُبَاءٍ، وَقَالَ الْآخَرُ: هُوَ مَسْجِدُ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: "هُوَ مَسْجِدِي هَذَا" تَفَرَّدَ بِهِ أَحْمَدُ.

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا إِسْحَاقُ بْنُ عِيسَى، حَدَّثَنَا لَيْثٌ، حَدَّثَنِي عِمْرَانُ بْنُ أَبِي أَنَسٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: تَمَارَى رَجُلَانِ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الَّذِي أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى مِنْ أَوَّلِ يَوْمٍ، فَقَالَ رَجُلٌ: هُوَ مَسْجِدُ قُبَاءٍ، وَقَالَ الْآخَرُ: هُوَ مَسْجِدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "هُوَ مَسْجِدِي".

وَكَذَا رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَالنَّسَائِيُّ عَنْ قُتَيْبَةَ، عَنِ اللَّيْثِ وَصَحَّحَهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ، وَرَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ كَمَا سَيَأْتِي.

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا يَحْيَى، عَنْ أُنَيْس بْنِ أَبِي يَحْيَى، حَدَّثَنِي أَبِي قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ أَبَا سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيَّ قَالَ: اخْتَلَفَ رَجُلَانِ: رَجُلٌ مِنْ بَنِي خَدْرة، وَرَجُلٌ مِنْ بَنِي عَمْرِو بْنِ عَوْفٍ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الَّذِي أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى، فَقَالَ الْخُدْرِيُّ: هُوَ مَسْجِدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ، وَقَالَ العَمْري: هُوَ مَسْجِدُ قُبَاءٍ، فَأَتَيَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ فَسَأَلَاهُ عَنْ ذَلِكَ، فَقَالَ: "هُوَ هَذَا الْمَسْجِدُ" لَمَسْجِدِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ، وَقَالَ: "فِي ذَاكَ [خَيْرٌ كَثِيرٌ] يَعْنِي: مَسْجِدَ قُبَاءٍ. 

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ أَبُو جَعْفَرِ بْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ بَشَّارٍ، حَدَّثَنَا يَحْيَى بْنُ سَعِيدٍ -حَدَّثَنَا حُمَيْدٌ الْخَرَّاطُ الْمَدَنِيُّ، سَأَلْتُ أَبَا سَلَمَةَ بْنَ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ فَقُلْتُ: كَيْفَ سَمِعْتُ أَبَاكَ يَقُولُ فِي الْمَسْجِدِ الَّذِي أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى؟ فَقَالَ أَبِي: أَتَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ فَدَخَلْتُ عَلَيْهِ فِي بَيْتٍ لِبَعْضِ نِسَائِهِ، فَقُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أَيْنَ الْمَسْجِدُ الَّذِي أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى؟ قَالَ: فَأَخَذَ كَفًّا مِنْ حَصْبَاءَ فَضَرَبَ بِهِ الْأَرْضَ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: "هُوَ مَسْجِدُكُمْ هَذَا". ثُمَّ قَالَ: [فقلتُ لَهُ: هَكَذَا] سمعتَ أَبَاكَ يَذْكُرُهُ؟.

رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ مُنْفَرِدًا بِهِ عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ حَاتِمٍ، عَنْ يَحْيَى بْنِ سَعِيدٍ، بِهِ وَرَوَاهُ عَنْ أَبِي بَكْرِ بن أَبِي شَيْبَةَ وَغَيْرِهِ، عَنْ حَاتِمِ بْنِ إِسْمَاعِيلَ، عَنْ حُمَيْدٍ الْخَرَّاطِ، بِهِ. 

وَقَدْ قَالَ بِأَنَّهُ مَسْجِدُ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ جَمَاعَةٌ مِنَ السَّلَفِ وَالْخَلَفِ، وَهُوَ مَرْوِيٌّ عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ الْخَطَّابِ، وَابْنِهِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، وَزَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ، وَسَعِيدِ بْنِ الْمُسَيَّبِ. وَاخْتَارَهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿لَمَسْجِدٌ أُسِّسَ عَلَى التَّقْوَى مِنْ أَوَّلِ يَوْمٍ أَحَقُّ أَنْ تَقُومَ فِيهِ فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُطَّهِّرِينَ﴾ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى اسْتِحْبَابِ الصَّلَاةِ فِي الْمَسَاجِدِ الْقَدِيمَةِ الْمُؤَسَّسَةِ مِنْ أَوَّلِ بِنَائِهَا عَلَى عِبَادَةِ اللَّهِ وَحْدَهُ لَا شَرِيكَ لَهُ، وَعَلَى اسْتِحْبَابِ الصَّلَاةِ مَعَ جَمَاعَةِ الصَّالِحِينَ، وَالْعِبَادِ الْعَامِلِينَ الْمُحَافِظِينَ عَلَى إِسْبَاغِ الْوُضُوءِ، وَالتَّنَزُّهِ عَنْ مُلَابَسَةِ الْقَاذُورَاتِ.

وَقَدْ قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ جَعْفَرٍ، عَنْ شُعْبَةَ، عَنْ عَبْدِ الْمَلِكِ بْنِ عُمَيْرٍ، سَمِعْتُ شَبِيبًا أَبَا رَوْحٍ يُحَدِّثُ عَنْ رَجُلٍ مِنْ أَصْحَابِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ؛ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ صَلَّى بِهِمُ الصُّبْحَ فَقَرَأَ بِهِمُ الرُّومَ فَأَوْهَمَ، فَلَمَّا انْصَرَفَ قَالَ: "إِنَّهُ يَلْبَسُ عَلَيْنَا الْقُرْآنُ، إِنْ أَقْوَامًا مِنْكُمْ يُصَلُّونَ مَعَنَا لَا يُحْسِنُونَ الْوُضُوءَ، فَمَنْ شَهِدَ الصَّلَاةَ مَعَنَا فَلْيُحْسِنِ الْوُضُوءَ".

ثُمَّ رَوَاهُ مِنْ طَرِيقَيْنِ آخَرَيْنِ، عَنْ عَبْدِ الْمَلِكِ بْنِ عُمَيْرٍ، عَنْ شَبِيبٍ أَبِي رَوْحٍ مِنْ ذِي الكَلاع: أَنَّهُ صَلَّى مَعَ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ، فَذَكَرَهُ فَدَلَّ هَذَا عَلَى أَنَّ إِكْمَالَ الطَّهَارَةِ يُسَهِّلُ الْقِيَامَ فِي الْعِبَادَةِ، وَيُعِينُ عَلَى إِتْمَامِهَا وَإِكْمَالِهَا وَالْقِيَامِ بِمَشْرُوعَاتِهَا.

وَقَالَ أَبُو الْعَالِيَةِ فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُطَّهِّرِينَ﴾ إِنَّ الطَّهُورَ بِالْمَاءِ لَحَسَنٌ، وَلَكِنَّهُمُ الْمُطَّهِّرُونَ مِنَ الذُّنُوبِ.

وَقَالَ الْأَعْمَشُ: التَّوْبَةُ مِنَ الذَّنْبِ، وَالتَّطْهِيرُ مِنَ الشِّرْكِ.

وَقَدْ وَرَدَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ الْمَرْوِيِّ مِنْ طُرُقٍ، فِي السُّنَنِ وَغَيْرِهَا، أَنَّ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال لِأَهْلِ قُبَاءٍ: "قَدْ أَثْنَى اللَّهُ عَلَيْكُمْ فِي الطَّهُورِ، فَمَاذَا تَصْنَعُونَ؟ " فَقَالُوا: نَسْتَنْجِي بِالْمَاءِ.

وَقَدْ قَالَ الْحَافِظُ أَبُو بَكْرٍ الْبَزَّارُ: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ شَبِيبٍ، حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ قَالَ: وَجَدْتُهُ فِي كِتَابِ أَبِي، عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، عَنْ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: نَزَلَتْ هَذِهِ الْآيَةُ فِي أَهْلِ قُبَاءٍ. ﴿فِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا وَاللَّهُ يُحِبُّ الْمُطَّهِّرِينَ﴾ فَسَأَلَهُمْ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ فَقَالُوا: إِنَّا نُتْبِعُ الْحِجَارَةَ الْمَاءَ.

ثُمَّ قَالَ: تَفَرَّدَ بِهِ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ، عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، ولم يرو عنه سوى ابنه. قُلْتُ: وَإِنَّمَا ذَكَرْتُهُ بِهَذَا اللَّفْظِ لِأَنَّهُ مَشْهُورٌ بَيْنَ الْفُقَهَاءِ وَلَمْ يَعْرِفْهُ كَثِيرٌ مِنَ الْمُحَدِّثِينَ الْمُتَأَخِّرِينَ، أَوْ كُلِّهُمْ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

---

## 9:109-110 — verses 109-110 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty says: he who founded his building upon fear of Allah and His good pleasure is not equal to one who built a mosque out of harmful intent, disbelief, and division among the believers, and as a lookout post for one who had previously warred against Allah and His Messenger. These people built their building only {on the brink of a crumbling bank}, that is, the edge of a pit, resembling {the fire of Hell, and Allah does not guide the wrongdoing people}, meaning: He does not set right the work of those who cause corruption.

Jabir ibn Abd Allah said: I saw the mosque that had been built out of harmful intent, smoke was coming out of it during the time of the Prophet ﷺ.

Ibn Jurayj said: it was mentioned to us that some men dug there and found smoke coming out of it. Qatadah said the same.

Khalaf ibn Yasin al-Kufi said: I saw the mosque of the hypocrites which Allah the Almighty mentioned in the Qur'an, and in it was a hole from which smoke was coming out, and it is today a dumping place for refuse. Ibn Jarir, may Allah have mercy on him, related this.

As for His saying, {The building which they built will not cease to be a source of doubt in their hearts}, that is: doubt and hypocrisy, because of their undertaking this disgraceful deed, which bequeathed to them hypocrisy in their hearts, just as the worshippers of the calf were made to drink love of it into their hearts.

As for His saying, {unless their hearts are torn to pieces}, that is: by their death. This was said by Ibn Abbas, Mujahid, Qatadah, Zayd ibn Aslam, al-Suddi, Habib ibn Abi Thabit, al-Dahhak, Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam, and more than one of the scholars of the earlier generations (al-salaf).

{And Allah is All-Knowing}, that is: of the deeds of His creation, {All-Wise} in requiting them for those deeds, whether good or evil.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى: لَا يَسْتَوِي مَنْ أَسَّسَ بُنْيَانَهُ عَلَى تَقْوَى اللَّهِ وَرِضْوَانٍ، وَمَنْ بَنَى مَسْجِدًا ضِرَارًا وَكُفْرًا وَتَفْرِيقًا بَيْنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ، وَإِرْصَادًا لِمَنْ حَارَبَ اللَّهَ وَرَسُولَهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ، فَإِنَّمَا بَنَى هَؤُلَاءِ بُنْيَانَهُمْ ﴿عَلَى شَفَا جُرُفٍ هَارٍ﴾ أَيْ: طَرَفِ حَفِيرة مِثَالُهُ ﴿فِي نَارِ جَهَنَّمَ وَاللَّهُ لَا يَهْدِي الْقَوْمَ الظَّالِمِينَ﴾ أَيْ: لَا يُصْلِحُ عَمَلَ الْمُفْسِدِينَ.

قَالَ جَابِرُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ: رَأَيْتُ الْمَسْجِدَ الَّذِي بُنِيَ ضِرَارًا يَخْرُجُ مِنْهُ الدُّخَانُ عَلَى عَهْدِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جُرَيْج ذُكر لَنَا أَنَّ رِجَالًا حَفَروا فَوَجَدُوا الدُّخَانَ يَخْرُجُ مِنْهُ. وَكَذَا قَالَ قَتَادَةُ.

وَقَالَ خَلَفُ بْنُ يَاسِينَ الْكُوفِيُّ: رَأَيْتُ مَسْجِدَ الْمُنَافِقِينَ الَّذِي ذَكَرَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى فِي الْقُرْآنِ، وَفِيهِ جَحَرٌ يَخْرُجُ مِنْهُ الدُّخَانُ، وَهُوَ الْيَوْمُ مَزْبلة. رَوَاهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿لَا يَزَالُ بُنْيَانُهُمُ الَّذِي بَنَوْا رِيبَةً فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ﴾ أَيْ: شَكًّا وَنِفَاقًا بِسَبَبِ إِقْدَامِهِمْ عَلَى هَذَا الصَّنِيعِ الشَّنِيعِ، أَوْرَثَهُمْ نِفَاقًا فِي قُلُوبِهِمْ، كَمَا أُشْرِبَ عَابِدُو الْعِجْلِ حُبَّهُ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿إِلا أَنْ تَقَطَّعَ قُلُوبُهُمْ﴾ أَيْ: بِمَوْتِهِمْ. قَالَهُ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ، وَمُجَاهِدٌ، وَقَتَادَةُ، وَزَيْدُ بْنُ أَسْلَمَ، وَالسُّدِّيُّ، وَحَبِيبُ بْنُ أَبِي ثَابِتٍ، وَالضَّحَّاكُ، وَعَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ، وَغَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ عُلَمَاءِ السَّلَفِ.

﴿وَاللَّهُ عَلِيمٌ﴾ أَيْ: بِأَعْمَالِ خَلْقِهِ، ﴿حَكِيمٌ﴾ فِي مُجَازَاتِهِمْ عَنْهَا، مِنْ خَيْرٍ وَشَرٍّ.

---

## 9:111 — verse 111

### Translation

The Almighty informs that He has compensated His believing servants for their souls and their wealth, since they offered these up in His path, with Paradise. This is part of His bounty, His generosity, and His favor, for He accepted a payment for something He already owns, out of His graciousness toward His obedient servants. This is why al-Hasan al-Basri and Qatadah said: "By God, He struck a bargain with them and paid a very high price for them."

Shamir ibn Atiyyah said: "There is no Muslim but that God, mighty and exalted, holds upon his neck a pledge of allegiance, which he must either fulfill or die upon." Then he recited this verse.

This is why it is said: "Whoever bears arms in the path of God has given his allegiance to God," meaning: God has accepted this contract and fulfilled it.

Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi and others said: Abdullah ibn Rawahah, may God be pleased with him, said to the Messenger of God ﷺ, referring to the night of al-'Aqabah: "Stipulate for your Lord and for yourself whatever you wish." He said: "I stipulate for my Lord that you worship Him and associate nothing with Him, and I stipulate for myself that you protect me as you protect your own selves and your wealth." They said: "And what do we have if we do that?" He said: "Paradise." They said: "The bargain has profited! We will not ask to cancel it, nor will we permit it to be cancelled." Then this verse was revealed: {Indeed, God has purchased from the believers their souls and their wealth} the verse.

His saying: {They fight in the path of God, so they kill and are killed}, meaning: whether they kill or are killed, or both of these occur for them, Paradise has become obligatory for them. This is why it comes in the two Sahihs: "God has guaranteed for whoever goes forth in His path, going forth for nothing but jihad in My path and belief in My messengers, that if He takes his life, He will admit him into Paradise, or that He will return him to the dwelling from which he set out, having attained whatever reward or spoils he attained."

His saying: {A promise binding upon Him, in the Torah, the Gospel, and the Qur'an} is a confirmation of this promise, and an announcement that He has written it upon His noble Self, and sent it down upon His messengers in His great books, namely the Torah revealed to Moses (peace be upon him), the Gospel revealed to Jesus (peace be upon him), and the Qur'an revealed to Muhammad ﷺ, the prayers and peace of God be upon them all.

His saying: {And who is more faithful to his covenant than God?} [meaning: and there is no one more perfectly faithful to what he has covenanted than God], for He never breaks His promise. This is like His saying: {And who is more truthful than God in speech?} [al-Nisa: 87] and {And who is more truthful than God in word?} [al-Nisa: 122]. This is why He said: {So rejoice in your transaction which you have concluded, and that is the great triumph}, meaning: let whoever fulfills the requirements of this contract and keeps this covenant rejoice in the great triumph and everlasting bliss.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يُخْبِرُ تَعَالَى أَنَّهُ عَاوَضَ عِبَادَهُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ عَنْ أَنْفُسِهِمْ وَأَمْوَالِهِمْ إِذْ بَذَلُوهَا فِي سَبِيلِهِ بِالْجَنَّةِ، وَهَذَا مِنْ فَضْلِهِ وَكَرَمِهِ وَإِحْسَانِهِ، فَإِنَّهُ قَبِلَ الْعِوَضَ عَمَّا يَمْلِكُهُ بِمَا تَفَضَّلَ بِهِ عَلَى عِبَادِهِ الْمُطِيعِينَ لَهُ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ الْحَسَنُ الْبَصْرِيُّ وَقَتَادَةُ: بَايَعَهُمْ وَاللَّهِ فَأَغْلَى ثَمَنَهُمْ.

وَقَالَ شَمِر بْنُ عَطِيَّةَ: مَا مِنْ مُسْلِمٍ إِلَّا وَلِلَّهِ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، فِي عُنُقه بَيْعَةٌ، وفَّى بِهَا أَوْ مَاتَ عَلَيْهَا، ثُمَّ تَلَا هَذِهِ الْآيَةَ.

وَلِهَذَا يُقَالُ: مَنْ حَمَلَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ بَايَعَ اللَّهَ، أَيْ: قَبِل هَذَا الْعَقْدَ وَوَفَّى بِهِ.

وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ كَعْبٍ القُرَظي وَغَيْرُهُ: قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ رَوَاحَةَ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، لِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ -يَعْنِي لَيْلَةَ العقبةِ -: اشْتَرِطْ لِرَبِّكَ وَلِنَفْسِكَ مَا شِئْتَ! فَقَالَ: "أَشْتَرِطُ لِرَبِّي أَنْ تَعْبُدُوهُ وَلَا تُشْرِكُوا بِهِ شَيْئًا، وَأَشْتَرِطُ لِنَفْسِي أَنْ تَمْنَعُونِي مِمَّا تَمْنَعُونَ مِنْهُ أَنْفُسَكُمْ وَأَمْوَالَكُمْ". قَالُوا: فَمَا لَنَا إِذَا فَعَلْنَا ذَلِكَ؟ قَالَ: "الْجَنَّةُ". قَالُوا: رَبِح البيعُ، لَا نُقِيل وَلَا نَسْتَقِيلُ، فَنَزَلَتْ: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ اشْتَرَى مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ أَنْفُسَهُمْ وَأَمْوَالَهُمْ﴾ الْآيَةَ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿يُقَاتِلُونَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَيَقْتُلُونَ وَيُقْتَلُونَ﴾ أَيْ: سَوَاءٌ قَتَلُوا أَوْ قُتلوا، أَوِ اجْتَمَعَ لَهُمْ هَذَا وَهَذَا، فَقَدْ وَجَبَتْ لَهُمُ الْجَنَّةُ؛ وَلِهَذَا جَاءَ فِي الصَّحِيحَيْنِ: "وَتَكَفَّلَ اللَّهُ لِمَنْ خَرَجَ فِي سَبِيلِهِ، لَا يُخْرِجُهُ إِلَّا جِهَادٌ فِي سَبِيلِي، وَتَصْدِيقٌ بِرُسُلِي، بِأَنْ تَوَفَّاهُ أَنْ يُدْخِلَهُ الْجَنَّةَ، أَوْ يُرْجِعَهُ إِلَى مَسْكَنِهِ الَّذِي خَرَجَ مِنْهُ، نَائِلًا مَا نَالَ مِنْ أَجْرٍ أَوْ غَنِيمَةٍ". 

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَعْدًا عَلَيْهِ حَقًّا فِي التَّوْرَاةِ وَالإنْجِيلِ وَالْقُرْآنِ﴾ تَأْكِيدٌ لِهَذَا الْوَعْدِ، وَإِخْبَارٌ بِأَنَّهُ قَدْ كَتَبَهُ عَلَى نَفْسِهِ الْكَرِيمَةِ، وَأَنْزَلَهُ عَلَى رُسُلِهِ فِي كُتُبِهِ الْكِبَارِ، وَهِيَ التَّوْرَاةُ الْمُنَزَّلَةُ عَلَى مُوسَى، وَالْإِنْجِيلُ الْمُنَزَّلُ عَلَى عِيسَى، وَالْقُرْآنُ الْمُنَزَّلُ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ، صَلَوَاتُ اللَّهِ وَسَلَامُهُ عَلَيْهِمْ أَجْمَعِينَ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَمَنْ أَوْفَى بِعَهْدِهِ مِنَ اللَّهِ﴾ [أَيْ: وَلَا وَاحِدَ أَعْظَمُ وَفَاءً بِمَا عَاهَدَ عَلَيْهِ مِنَ اللَّهِ] فَإِنَّهُ لَا يُخْلِفُ الْمِيعَادِ، وَهَذَا كَقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿وَمَنْ أَصْدَقُ مِنَ اللهِ حَدِيثًا﴾ [النِّسَاءِ: ٨٧] ﴿وَمَنْ أَصْدَقُ مِنَ اللَّهِ قِيلا﴾ [النِّسَاءِ: ١٢٢] ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿فَاسْتَبْشِرُوا بِبَيْعِكُمُ الَّذِي بَايَعْتُمْ بِهِ وَذَلِكَ هُوَ الْفَوْزُ الْعَظِيمُ﴾ أَيْ: فَلْيَسْتَبْشِرْ مَنْ قَامَ بِمُقْتَضَى هَذَا الْعَقْدِ وَوَفَى بِهَذَا الْعَهْدِ، بِالْفَوْزِ الْعَظِيمِ، والنعيم المقيم.

---

## 9:112 — verse 112

### Translation

This is the description of the believers from whom Allah has purchased their souls and their wealth, for these beautiful qualities and noble traits: {those who repent} from all sins, those who abandon indecent acts, {those who worship} meaning those who carry out worship of their Lord, maintaining it steadfastly, which consists of sayings and deeds. Among the most distinguished of sayings is praise, and therefore He said {those who praise}. And among the most excellent of deeds is fasting, which is the abandonment of pleasures such as food, drink, and intercourse, and this is what is meant by "al-siyaha" (journeying/wandering) here. Therefore He said {those who journey}, just as He described the wives of the Prophet ﷺ with this in His saying: {sa'ihat} [al-Tahrim: 5], meaning fasting women. Likewise bowing and prostration, which are expressions referring to prayer, and therefore He said {those who bow, those who prostrate}. Along with this they benefit the creation of Allah and guide them toward obedience to Allah by enjoining what is right upon them and forbidding what is wrong, together with knowledge of what ought to be done and what must be avoided, which is safeguarding the limits set by Allah in what He has permitted and what He has forbidden, both in knowledge and in practice. Thus they carry out the worship due to the Truth and sincere concern for creation. Therefore He said {and give glad tidings to the believers}, because faith encompasses all of this, and true happiness, complete happiness, belongs to whoever is characterized by it.

[Clarification that what is meant by al-siyaha is fasting]

Sufyan al-Thawri said, from Asim, from Zirr, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who said: {those who journey} means those who fast. The same has been related from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, and from al-Awfi from Ibn Abbas.

Ali ibn Abi Talha said, from Ibn Abbas: whenever Allah mentions "al-siyaha" in the Qur'an, it refers to those who fast. Al-Dahhak, may Allah have mercy on him, said the same.

Ibn Jarir said: [chain] Ibrahim ibn Yazid, from al-Walid ibn Abdullah, from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, who said: the siyaha of this nation is fasting.

Likewise Mujahid, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, Ata, Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami, al-Dahhak ibn Muzahim, Sufyan ibn Uyayna and others said that what is meant by "those who journey" is those who fast.

Al-Hasan al-Basri said: {those who journey} means those who fast the month of Ramadan.

Abu Amr al-Abdi said: {those who journey} means those among the believers who fast continually.

Something similar has come in a marfu (elevated) hadith. Ibn Jarir said: [chain] Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Bazi', Hakim ibn Hizam, Sulayman, from Abu Salih, from Abu Hurayra, who said: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, "Those who journey are those who fast."

[Then he related it from Bundar, from Ibn Mahdi, from Isra'il, from Sulayman al-A'mash, from Abu Salih, from Abu Hurayra, that he said: {those who journey} means those who fast.]

This mawquf (halted) version is more authentic.

He also said: [chain] Yunus, from Ibn Wahb, from Umar ibn al-Harith, from Amr ibn Dinar, from Ubayd ibn Umayr, who said: the Prophet ﷺ was asked about "those who journey" and he said, "They are those who fast."

This is a good mursal (chain missing the companion link) report.

These are the most authentic and most well-known of the sayings. There has also come something indicating that "al-siyaha" means jihad, which is what Abu Dawud related in his Sunan, from the hadith of Abu Umama, that a man said: O Messenger of Allah, permit me to go on siyaha (journeying). The Prophet ﷺ said, "The siyaha of my nation is jihad in the path of Allah."

Ibn al-Mubarak said, from Ibn Lahi'a: Umara ibn Ghaziyya informed me that siyaha was mentioned in the presence of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, "Allah has replaced that for us with jihad in the path of Allah, and saying 'Allahu Akbar' upon every elevated place."

From Ikrima it is said: they are the seekers of knowledge. Abd al-Rahman ibn Zayd ibn Aslam said: they are the emigrants (al-muhajirun). Both of these were related by Ibn Abi Hatim.

What is meant by "al-siyaha" is not what some who worship through mere wandering upon the earth may understand it to be, nor isolating oneself upon towering mountain peaks, in caves, and in wilderness, for this is not something legislated except during days of turmoil and religious upheaval, as is established in Sahih al-Bukhari, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "It is about to be that the best wealth of a man will be sheep which he follows to the peaks of mountains and places where rain falls, fleeing with his religion from the turmoils."

Al-Awfi and Ali ibn Abi Talha said, from Ibn Abbas, regarding His saying {and those who observe the limits of Allah}: he said, those who carry out obedience to Allah. Al-Hasan al-Basri said the same, and in another report from him: {and those who observe the limits of Allah} he said, meaning the obligations of Allah, and in another report: those who stand firm upon the command of Allah.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

هَذَا نعتُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ الَّذِينَ اشْتَرَى اللَّهُ مِنْهُمْ أَنْفُسَهُمْ وَأَمْوَالَهُمْ بِهَذِهِ الصِّفَاتِ الْجَمِيلَةِ وَالْخِلَالِ الْجَلِيلَةِ: ﴿التَّائِبُونَ﴾ مِنَ الذُّنُوبِ كُلِّهَا، التَّارِكُونَ لِلْفَوَاحِشِ، ﴿الْعَابِدُونَ﴾ أَيْ: الْقَائِمُونَ بِعِبَادَةِ رَبِّهِمْ مُحَافِظِينَ عَلَيْهَا، وَهِيَ الْأَقْوَالُ وَالْأَفْعَالُ فَمِنْ أخَصّ الْأَقْوَالِ الْحَمْدُ ؛ فَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿الْحَامِدُونَ﴾ وَمِنْ أَفْضَلِ الْأَعْمَالِ الصيامُ، وَهُوَ تَرْكُ الملاذِّ مِنَ الطَّعَامِ وَالشَّرَابِ وَالْجِمَاعِ، وَهُوَ الْمُرَادُ بِالسِّيَاحَةِ هَاهُنَا؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿السَّائِحُونَ﴾ كَمَا وَصَفَ أَزْوَاجَ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ بِذَلِكَ فِي قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿سَائِحَاتٍ﴾ [التَّحْرِيمِ: ٥] أَيْ: صَائِمَاتٍ، وَكَذَا الرُّكُوعُ وَالسُّجُودُ، وَهُمَا عِبَارَةٌ عَنِ الصَّلَاةِ، وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿الرَّاكِعُونَ السَّاجِدُونَ﴾ وَهُمْ مَعَ ذَلِكَ يَنْفَعُونَ خَلْقَ اللَّهِ، وَيُرْشِدُونَهُمْ إِلَى طَاعَةِ اللَّهِ بِأَمْرِهِمْ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ وَنَهْيِهِمْ عَنِ الْمُنْكَرِ، مَعَ الْعِلْمِ بِمَا يَنْبَغِي فِعْلُهُ وَيَجِبُ تركُه، وَهُوَ حِفْظُ حُدُودِ اللَّهِ فِي تَحْلِيلِهِ وَتَحْرِيمِهِ، عِلْمًا وَعَمَلًا فَقَامُوا بِعِبَادَةِ الْحَقِّ وَنُصْحِ الْخُلُقِ؛ وَلِهَذَا قَالَ: ﴿وَبَشِّرِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ﴾ لِأَنَّ الْإِيمَانَ يَشْمَلُ هَذَا كُلَّهُ، وَالسَّعَادَةُ كُلُّ السَّعَادَةِ لِمَنِ اتَّصَفَ بِهِ.

[بَيَانُ أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالسِّيَاحَةِ الصِّيَامُ] : 

قَالَ سُفْيَانُ الثَّوْرِيُّ، عَنْ عَاصِمٍ، عَنْ زِرّ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: ﴿السَّائِحُونَ﴾ الصَّائِمُونَ. وَكَذَا رُوي عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَير، وَالْعَوْفِيُّ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ.

وَقَالَ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: كُلَّ مَا ذَكَرَ اللَّهُ فِي الْقُرْآنِ السِّيَاحَةَ، هُمُ الصَّائِمُونَ. وَكَذَا قَالَ الضَّحَّاكُ، رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ.

وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو أَحْمَدَ، حَدَّثَنَا إِبْرَاهِيمُ بْنُ يَزِيدَ، عَنِ الْوَلِيدِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنْ عَائِشَةَ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، قَالَتْ: سياحةُ هَذِهِ الْأُمَّةِ الصِّيَامُ. 

وَهَكَذَا قَالَ مُجَاهِدٌ، وَسَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَير، وَعَطَاءٌ، وَأَبُو عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ السُّلَمِيُّ، وَالضَّحَّاكُ بْنُ مُزاحم، وَسُفْيَانُ بْنُ عُيينة وَغَيْرُهُمْ: أَنَّ الْمُرَادَ بِالسَّائِحِينَ: الصَّائِمُونَ.

وَقَالَ الْحَسَنُ الْبَصْرِيُّ: ﴿السَّائِحُونَ﴾ الصَّائِمُونَ شَهْرَ رَمَضَانَ.

وَقَالَ أَبُو عَمْرٍو العَبْدي: ﴿السَّائِحُونَ﴾ الَّذِينَ يُدِيمُونَ الصِّيَامَ مِنَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ.

وَقَدْ وَرَدَ فِي حَدِيثٍ مَرْفُوعٍ نَحْوَ هَذَا، وَقَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنِي مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بن بَزِيع، حَدَّثَنَا حَكِيمُ بْنُ حِزَامٍ، حَدَّثَنَا سُلَيْمَانُ، عَنْ أَبِي صَالِحٍ، عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "السَّائِحُونَ هُمُ الصَّائِمُونَ" 

[ثُمَّ رَوَاهُ عَنْ بُنْدَار، عَنِ ابْنِ مَهْدِيٍّ، عَنْ إِسْرَائِيلَ، عَنْ سُلَيْمَانَ الْأَعْمَشِ، عَنْ أَبِي صَالِحٍ، عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: ﴿السَّائِحُونَ﴾ الصَّائِمُونَ] . 

وَهَذَا الْمَوْقُوفُ أَصَحُّ.

وَقَالَ أَيْضًا: حَدَّثَنِي يُونُسُ، عَنِ ابْنِ وَهْبٍ، عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ الْحَارِثِ، عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ دِينَارٍ، عَنْ عُبَيد بْنِ عُمَير قَالَ: سُئِلَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ عَنِ السَّائِحِينَ فَقَالَ: "هُمُ الصَّائِمُونَ". 

وَهَذَا مُرْسَلٌ جَيِّدٌ.

فَهَذِهِ أَصَحُّ الْأَقْوَالِ وَأَشْهَرُهَا، وَجَاءَ مَا يَدُلُّ عَلَى أَنَّ السِّيَاحَةَ الْجِهَادُ، وَهُوَ مَا رَوَى أَبُو دَاوُدَ فِي سُنَنِهِ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ أَبِي أُمَامَةَ أَنَّ رَجُلًا قَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، ائْذَنْ لِي فِي السِّيَاحَةِ. فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: "سِيَاحَةُ أُمَّتَيِ الْجِهَادُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ". 

وَقَالَ ابْنُ الْمُبَارَكِ، عَنِ ابْنِ لَهِيعة: أَخْبَرَنِي عُمارة بْنُ غَزِيَّة: أَنَّ السِّيَاحَةَ ذُكِرَتْ عِنْدَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "أَبْدَلَنَا اللَّهُ بِذَلِكَ الْجِهَادَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ، وَالتَّكْبِيرَ عَلَى كُلِّ شَرَفٍ". 

وَعَنْ عِكْرِمة أَنَّهُ قَالَ: هُمْ طَلَبَةُ الْعِلْمِ. وَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ: هُمُ الْمُهَاجِرُونَ. رَوَاهُمَا ابْنُ أَبِي حَاتِمٍ.

وَلَيْسَ الْمُرَادُ مِنَ السِّيَاحَةِ مَا قَدْ يَفْهَمُهُ بَعْضُ مَنْ يَتَعَبَّدُ بِمُجَرَّدِ السِّيَاحَةِ فِي الْأَرْضِ، وَالتَّفَرُّدِ فِي شَوَاهِقِ الْجِبَالِ وَالْكُهُوفِ وَالْبَرَارِي، فَإِنَّ هَذَا لَيْسَ بِمَشْرُوعٍ إِلَّا فِي أَيَّامِ الفتَن وَالزَّلَازِلِ فِي الدِّينِ، كَمَا ثَبَتَ فِي صَحِيحِ الْبُخَارِيِّ، عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: "يُوشِكُ أَنْ يَكُونَ خَيْرَ مَالِ الرَّجُلِ غَنَم يَتْبَع بِهَا شَعفَ الْجِبَالِ، وَمَوَاقِعَ القَطْر، يَفِرُّ بِدِينِهِ مِنَ الْفِتَنِ". 

وَقَالَ الْعَوْفِيُّ وَعَلِيُّ بْنُ أَبِي طَلْحَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: ﴿وَالْحَافِظُونَ لِحُدُودِ اللَّهِ﴾ قَالَ: الْقَائِمُونَ بِطَاعَةِ اللَّهِ. وَكَذَا قَالَ الْحَسَنُ الْبَصْرِيُّ، وَعَنْهُ رِوَايَةُ: ﴿وَالْحَافِظُونَ لِحُدُودِ اللَّهِ﴾ قال: لفرائض اللَّهِ، وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ: الْقَائِمُونَ عَلَى أَمْرِ اللَّهِ.

---

## 9:113-114 — verses 113-114 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Imam Ahmad said: Abd al-Razzaq related to us, Ma'mar related to us, from al-Zuhri, from Ibn al-Musayyab, from his father, who said: When death approached Abu Talib, the Prophet ﷺ came in to him, and with him were Abu Jahl and Abdullah ibn Abi Umayyah. He said: "O uncle, say: there is no god but Allah, a word by which I may argue on your behalf before Allah, mighty and majestic is He." Abu Jahl and Abdullah ibn Abi Umayyah said: "O Abu Talib, do you turn away from the religion of Abd al-Muttalib?" [He said: They continued speaking to him until the last thing he said to them was: "On the religion of Abd al-Muttalib."] The Prophet ﷺ said: "I will surely ask forgiveness for you as long as I am not forbidden to do so." Then this was revealed: {It is not for the Prophet and those who believe to ask forgiveness for the polytheists, even if they be near of kin, after it has become clear to them that they are companions of the Blazing Fire}. He said: And also revealed concerning him was: {Indeed, you cannot guide whom you love} [al-Qasas: 56]. Both al-Bukhari and Muslim reported it.

Imam Ahmad also said: Yahya ibn Adam related to us, Sufyan informed us, from Abu Ishaq, from Abu al-Khalil, from Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: I heard a man asking forgiveness for his parents while they were polytheists. I said: "Does a man ask forgiveness for his parents while they are polytheists?" He said: "Did not Abraham ask forgiveness for his father?" So I mentioned that to the Prophet ﷺ, and this was revealed: {It is not for the Prophet and those who believe to ask forgiveness for the polytheists} up to His saying: {but when it became clear to him that he was an enemy of Allah}. He said: "When he died." I do not know whether Sufyan said it, or Isra'il said it, or whether it is part of the hadith: "When he died."

I say: this is established from Mujahid, that he said: "When he died."

Imam Ahmad also said: al-Hasan ibn Musa related to us, Zuhayr related to us, Zubayd ibn al-Harith al-Yami related to us, from Muharib ibn Dithar, from Ibn Buraydah, from his father, who said: We were with the Prophet ﷺ, and he stopped with us, and we with him were nearly a thousand riders. He prayed two rak'ahs, then turned his face toward us with his eyes shedding tears. Umar ibn al-Khattab stood up to him, offering his father and mother as ransom for him, and said: "O Messenger of Allah, what is the matter with you?" He said: "I asked my Lord, mighty and majestic is He, for permission to ask forgiveness for my mother, but He did not grant me permission, and my eyes wept out of mercy for her because of the Fire. And I had forbidden you three things: I forbade you to visit graves, so visit them, for visiting them will remind you of good. And I forbade you the meat of sacrificial animals after three days, so eat and withhold as you wish. And I forbade you vessels for drinks, so drink from any vessel, but do not drink anything intoxicating."

Ibn Jarir related, from the hadith of Alqamah ibn Marthad, from Sulayman ibn Buraydah, from his father: that when the Messenger of Allah ﷺ came to Mecca, he came to the outline of a grave and sat by it, and began speaking, then stood up weeping. We said: "O Messenger of Allah, what you have done has troubled us." He said: "I asked my Lord's permission to visit my mother's grave, and He gave me permission, and I asked His permission to seek forgiveness for her, but He did not give me permission." He was never seen weeping more than on that day.

Ibn Abi Hatim said in his tafsir: My father related to us, Khalid ibn Khidash related to us, Abdullah ibn Wahb related to us, from Ibn Jurayj, from Ayyub ibn Hani', from Masruq, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ went out one day to the graveyards, and we followed him. He came and sat by a grave among them, and spoke to it quietly for a long time, then wept, and we wept because of his weeping. Then he stood up, and Umar ibn al-Khattab stood up to him. He called him, then called us, and said: "What made you weep?" We said: "We wept because you wept." He said: "The grave beside which I sat is the grave of Aminah, and I asked my Lord's permission to visit her, and He gave me permission." Then he related it through another chain, then mentioned from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud something close to it, in which it says: "And I asked my Lord's permission to pray for her, but He did not give me permission, and He revealed to me: {It is not for the Prophet and those who believe to ask forgiveness for the polytheists, even if they be near of kin}. Then what a child feels for his mother overtook me, and I had forbidden you to visit graves, so visit them, for they remind one of the Hereafter."

Another hadith of similar meaning: al-Tabarani said: Muhammad ibn Ali al-Marwazi related to us, Abu al-Darda Abd al-Aziz ibn Munib related to us, Ishaq ibn Abdullah ibn Kaysan related to us, from his father, from Ikrimah, from Ibn Abbas: that when the Messenger of Allah ﷺ returned from the expedition of Tabuk and performed umrah, and when he descended from the mountain pass of Usfan, he commanded his companions: "Rest by the pass until I return to you." He went and stopped at his mother's grave, and spoke quietly to his Lord for a long time, then he wept, and his weeping grew intense, and those men wept because of his weeping. They said: "The Prophet of Allah has not wept in this place except that something has occurred among his community that it cannot bear." When these men wept, he rose and returned to them and said: "What makes you weep?" They said: "O Prophet of Allah, we wept because you wept, and we thought that perhaps something had occurred among your community that it could not bear." He said: "No, though part of it has occurred. But I stopped at my mother's grave and asked Allah to permit me to intercede for her on the Day of Resurrection, and Allah refused to permit me. I felt mercy for her, since she was my mother, and I wept. Then Gabriel came to me and said: {And the request of Abraham for forgiveness for his father was only because of a promise he had made to him. But when it became clear to him that he was an enemy of Allah, he disowned him} so disown your mother, just as Abraham disowned his father. I felt mercy for her, since she was my mother, and I asked my Lord to lift four things from my community, and He lifted two of them from them, and refused to lift two of them. I asked my Lord to lift from them stoning from the sky and drowning from the earth, and that He not clothe them in factions, and that He not make some of them taste the violence of others. Allah lifted from them stoning from the sky and drowning from the earth, but Allah refused to lift from them killing and turmoil." The reason he turned aside to his mother's grave is that she was buried beneath Kada, and Usfan belonged to them.

This is a gharib (singular) hadith and a strange narrative sequence. Stranger than it and even more objectionable is what al-Khatib al-Baghdadi related in his book "al-Sabiq wa al-Lahiq," with an unknown chain, from Aishah, in a hadith containing the story that Allah brought his mother back to life, so she believed, then returned to death. Likewise is what al-Suhayli related in "al-Rawd," with a chain containing a group of unknown narrators: that Allah brought back to life for him his father and his mother, and they believed in him.

Al-Hafiz Ibn Dihyah said: [This hadith is fabricated; the Qur'an and consensus reject it. Allah, exalted is He, said: {nor those who die while they are disbelievers} [al-Nisa: 18]. Abu Abdullah al-Qurtubi said: What this hadith necessarily implies... and he responded to Ibn Dihyah] on this argument, the substance of which is: that this was a new life, just as the sun returned after its setting, so Ali prayed the Asr prayer. Al-Tahawi said: it is an established [hadith], meaning the hadith of the sun.

Al-Qurtubi said: bringing the two of them back to life is not impossible, neither rationally nor by the Sacred Law. He said: I have heard that Allah brought his uncle Abu Talib back to life, and he believed in him. I say: all of this depends upon the authenticity of the hadith; if it is authentic, there is no obstacle to it, and Allah knows best.

Al-Awfi said, from Ibn Abbas, concerning His saying: {It is not for the Prophet and those who believe to ask forgiveness for the polytheists} the verse: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ wanted to ask forgiveness for his mother, so Allah forbade him from that. He said: "But Abraham, the intimate friend of Allah, asked forgiveness for his father." So Allah revealed: {And the request of Abraham for forgiveness for his father was only because of a promise he had made to him} the verse.

Ali ibn Abi Talhah said, from Ibn Abbas, concerning this verse: They used to ask forgiveness for them until this verse was revealed. When [it was revealed, they refrained from asking forgiveness for their dead, but he did not forbid them from asking forgiveness for the living until they died]. Then Allah revealed: {And the request of Abraham for forgiveness for his father} the verse.

Qatadah said concerning this verse: It was mentioned to us that some men among the companions of the Prophet ﷺ said: "O Prophet of Allah, among our fathers were those who treated neighbors well, maintained ties of kinship, freed the captive, and fulfilled their pledges. Shall we not ask forgiveness for them?" The Prophet ﷺ said: "Indeed, by Allah, I will ask forgiveness for my father just as Abraham asked forgiveness for his father." So Allah revealed: {It is not for the Prophet and those who believe to ask forgiveness for the polytheists} up to {the Blazing Fire}. Then Allah, exalted is He, excused Abraham, saying: {And the request of Abraham for forgiveness for his father was only because of a promise he had made to him. But when it became clear to him that he was an enemy of Allah, he disowned him}.

He said: it was mentioned to us that the Prophet of God said: "Certain words were revealed to me, and they entered into my ear and settled firmly in my heart: I was commanded not to seek forgiveness for one who died as a mushrik (polytheist), and whoever gives away the surplus of his wealth, that is better for him, and whoever withholds it, that is worse for him, and God does not blame for sufficiency (kafaf, having only enough to meet one's needs)."

Al-Thawri said, from al-Shaybani, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, who said: a Jewish man died and he had a Muslim son who did not go out with him (in the funeral procession). This was mentioned to Ibn 'Abbas, and he said: it was proper for him to walk with him and bury him, and to pray for his righteousness as long as he was alive, but once he died, he should leave his affair to him. Then he said: {And Ibrahim's asking forgiveness for his father was only because of a promise he had made to him, but when it became clear to him that he was an enemy of God, he disowned him}. He did not pray for him.

[I say] this is corroborated in soundness by what Abu Dawud and others related, from 'Ali ibn Abi Talib, who said: when Abu Talib died, I said: "O Messenger of God, your uncle, the misguided old man, has died." He said: "Go and bury him, and do not do anything new until you come back to me." And he mentioned the rest of the hadith.

It is also related that when the funeral bier of his uncle Abu Talib passed by the Messenger of God ﷺ, he said: "Kinship reached you, O uncle." 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah said: I would never refrain from praying over anyone among the people of the qiblah, even if she were an Abyssinian woman pregnant from fornication, because I have not heard that God withheld the prayer except from the mushrikin (polytheists). God, Mighty and Majestic, says: {It is not for the Prophet and those who believe to seek forgiveness for the mushrikin}.

Ibn Jarir related, from Ibn Waki', from his father, from 'Isma ibn Zamil, from his father, who said: I heard Abu Hurayrah say: "May God have mercy on a man who sought forgiveness for Abu Hurayrah and for his mother." I said: "And for his father?" He said: "No." He said: "My father died as a mushrik."

Concerning His saying: {but when it became clear to him that he was an enemy of God, he disowned him}, Ibn 'Abbas said: Ibrahim continued to seek forgiveness for his father until he died, and when it became clear to him that he was an enemy of God, he disowned him. In another report: when he died, it became clear to him that he was an enemy of God.

Mujahid, al-Dahhak, Qatadah and others, may God have mercy on them, said likewise.

'Ubayd ibn 'Umayr and Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: he will disown him on the Day of Resurrection, when he meets his father and his father's face is covered with dust and darkness, and he will say: "O Ibrahim, I used to disobey you, but today I will not disobey you." He will say: "O my Lord, did You not promise me that You would not disgrace me on the Day when they are resurrected? What disgrace could be greater than my father, the most distant one?" It will be said to him: "Look behind you." And there he is, a hyena smeared with filth, that is, he has been transformed into a hyena. Then he is dragged by his paws and thrown into the Fire.

Concerning His saying: {Indeed Ibrahim was truly aware (lawwah), forbearing (halim)}, Sufyan al-Thawri and more than one other said, from 'Asim ibn Bahdalah, from Zirr ibn Hubaysh, from 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, that he said: al-awwah is the one who prays much (al-dua'). It is likewise related through other channels from Ibn Mas'ud.

Ibn Jarir said: al-Muthanna told me: al-Hajjaj ibn Minhal told us: 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Bahram told us: Shahr ibn Hawshab told us, from 'Abdullah ibn Shaddad ibn al-Had, who said: while the Messenger of God ﷺ was sitting, a man said: "O Messenger of God, what is al-awwah?" He said: "The one who supplicates humbly (al-mutadarri')." He said: {Indeed Ibrahim was truly al-awwah, forbearing}.

Ibn Abi Hatim related it from the hadith of Ibn al-Mubarak, from 'Abd al-Hamid ibn Bahram, with the same chain, saying: al-mutadarri' is the one who prays much (al-dua').

Al-Thawri said, from Salamah ibn Kuhayl, from Muslim al-Batin, from Abu al-'Ubaydayn, that he asked Ibn Mas'ud about al-awwah, and he said: it is the merciful one (al-rahim).

Mujahid, Abu Maysarah 'Amr ibn Shurahbil, al-Hasan al-Basri and Qatadah said the same: that it is al-rahim, that is, merciful toward the servants of God.

Ibn al-Mubarak said, from Khalid, from 'Ikrimah, from Ibn 'Abbas, who said: al-awwah is the one certain in faith (al-muqin), in the language of Abyssinia. Al-'Awfi likewise said, from Ibn 'Abbas: that it is al-muqin. Mujahid and al-Dahhak said likewise. 'Ali ibn Abi Talhah and Mujahid said, from Ibn 'Abbas: al-awwah is the believer (al-mu'min), 'Ali ibn Abi Talhah adding from him: the believer who turns much in repentance (al-tawwab). Al-'Awfi said from him: he is the believer, in the language of Abyssinia. Ibn Jurayj likewise said: he is the believer, in the language of Abyssinia.

Ahmad said: Musa told us: Ibn Lahi'ah told us, from al-Harith ibn Yazid, from 'Ali ibn Rabah, from 'Uqbah ibn 'Amir: that the Messenger of God ﷺ said about a man called "Dhu al-Bijadayn": "Indeed he is awwah," and this was because he was a man who mentioned God much through the Qur'an and raised his voice in supplication.

Ibn Jarir related it as well.

Sa'id ibn Jubayr and al-Sha'bi said: al-awwah is the one who glorifies God much (al-musabbih). Ibn Wahb said, from Mu'awiyah ibn Salih, from Abu al-Zahiriyyah, from Jubayr ibn Nufayr, from Abu al-Darda', may God be pleased with him, who said: none preserves the practice of the mid-morning prayer (subhat al-duha) except an awwah. Shufayy ibn Mani' said, from Ayyub: al-awwah is the one who, when he remembers his sins, seeks forgiveness for them.

And from Mujahid: al-awwah is the watchful one, fearful, who commits a sin secretly, then repents of it secretly.

Ibn Abi Hatim, may God have mercy on him, mentioned all of this.

Ibn Jarir said: Ibn Waki' told us: al-Muharibi told us, from Hajjaj, from al-Hakam, from al-Hasan ibn Muslim ibn Yannaq: that a man used to mention God much and glorify Him, and this was mentioned to the Prophet ﷺ, and he said: "Indeed he is awwah."

He also said: Abu Kurayb told us: Ibn Yaman told us: al-Minhal ibn Khalifah told us, from Hajjaj ibn Artah, from 'Ata', from Ibn 'Abbas: that the Prophet ﷺ buried a deceased person and said: "May God have mercy on you, indeed you were truly awwah," meaning: much a reciter of the Qur'an.

Shu'bah said, from Abu Yunus al-Bahili, who said: I heard a man in Mecca, originally a Roman and a storyteller, narrating from Abu Dharr, who said: there was a man who used to circle the Sacred House and say in his supplication: "Awwih, awwih," and this was mentioned to the Prophet ﷺ, and he said: "Indeed he is awwah." He said: then I went out one night, and there was the Messenger of God ﷺ burying that man at night, with a lamp with him.

This is a gharib (singular) hadith, related by Ibn Jarir, who let it pass without objection.

It is related from Ka'b al-Ahbar that he said, concerning {Indeed Ibrahim was truly awwah}: he said: whenever he mentioned the Fire he would say: "Awwih, from the Fire."

Ibn Jurayj said, from Ibn 'Abbas: {Indeed Ibrahim was truly awwah}, he said: a jurist (faqih).

The learned imam Abu Ja'far ibn Jarir said: the most fitting of these sayings is the saying of the one who said that it means the one who prays much, and this fits the context, because God, exalted is He, when He mentioned that Ibrahim sought forgiveness for his father only because of a promise he had made to him, Ibrahim was indeed one who prayed much, forbearing toward whoever wronged him and caused him harm. For this reason he sought forgiveness for his father despite the severity of the harm his father did to him, in his saying: {Do you turn away from my gods, O Ibrahim? If you do not stop, I will surely stone you, so leave me for a long while. He said: Peace be upon you, I will seek forgiveness for you from my Lord, indeed He is ever gracious to me} [Maryam: 46, 47]. So he was forbearing toward him despite the harm he did to him, and he prayed for him and sought forgiveness for him. This is why the Exalted said: {Indeed Ibrahim was truly awwah, forbearing}.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، حَدَّثَنَا مَعْمَر، عَنِ الزَّهْرِيِّ، عَنِ ابْنِ الْمُسَيَّبِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: لَمَّا حَضَرت أَبَا طَالِبٍ الْوَفَاةُ دَخَلَ عَلَيْهِ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ وَعِنْدَهُ أَبُو جَهْلٍ، وَعَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ أَبِي أُمَيَّةَ، فَقَالَ: "أيْ عَمّ، قُلْ: لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ. كَلِمَةٌ أُحَاجُّ لَكَ بِهَا عِنْدَ اللَّهِ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ". فَقَالَ أَبُو جَهْلٍ وَعَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ أَبِي أُمَيَّةَ: يَا أَبَا طَالِبٍ، أَتَرْغَبُ عَنْ ملَّة عَبْدِ الْمُطَّلِبِ؟ [قَالَ: فَلَمْ يَزَالَا يُكَلِّمَانِهِ، حَتَّى قَالَ آخَرُ شَيْءٍ كَلَّمَهُمْ بِهِ: عَلَى مِلَّةِ عَبْدِ الْمُطَّلِبِ] . فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: "لَأَسْتَغْفِرَنَّ لَكَ مَا لَمْ أُنْهَ عَنْكَ". فَنَزَلَتْ: ﴿مَا كَانَ لِلنَّبِيِّ وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَنْ يَسْتَغْفِرُوا لِلْمُشْرِكِينَ وَلَوْ كَانُوا أُولِي قُرْبَى مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُمْ أَنَّهُمْ أَصْحَابُ الْجَحِيمِ﴾ قَالَ: وَنَزَلَتْ فِيهِ: ﴿إِنَّكَ لَا تَهْدِي مَنْ أَحْبَبْتَ﴾ [الْقَصَصِ: ٥٦] أَخْرَجَاهُ. 

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا يَحْيَى بْنُ آدَمَ، أَخْبَرَنَا سُفْيَانُ، عَنْ أَبِي إِسْحَاقَ، عَنْ أَبِي الْخَلِيلِ، عَنْ عَلِيٍّ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَجُلًا يَسْتَغْفِرُ لِأَبَوَيْهِ، وَهُمَا مُشْرِكَانِ، فَقُلْتُ: أَيَسْتَغْفِرُ الرجل لأبويه وهما مشركان؟ فقال: أو لم يَسْتَغْفِرْ إِبْرَاهِيمُ لِأَبِيهِ؟ فَذَكَرْتُ ذَلِكَ لِلنَّبِيِّ ﷺ، فَنَزَلَتْ: ﴿مَا كَانَ لِلنَّبِيِّ وَالَّذِينَ آمَنُوا أَنْ يَسْتَغْفِرُوا لِلْمُشْرِكِينَ﴾ إِلَى قَوْلِهِ: ﴿فَلَمَّا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ أَنَّهُ عَدُوٌّ لِلَّهِ﴾ قَالَ: "لَمَّا مَاتَ"، فَلَا أَدْرِي قَالَهُ سُفْيَانُ أَوْ قَالَهُ إِسْرَائِيلُ، أَوْ هُوَ فِي الْحَدِيثِ "لَمَّا مَاتَ". 

قُلْتُ هَذَا ثَابِتٌ عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: لَمَّا مَاتَ.
